Scheduler Bind Plugin (pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/defaultbinder/default_binder.go)\\nThe `DefaultBinder` plugin implements the `BindPlugin` interface and executes the actual binding. API Server Binding Handler (pkg/registry/core/pod/storage/storage.go)\\nThe `BindingREST` type implements the REST endpoint for pod binding. Its `Create()` method (lines 172-197):\\n- Validates the binding object\\n- Calls `r.assignPod()` to perform the actual binding\\n- The `assignPod()` method (lines 259-268) delegates to `setPodHostAndAnnotations()` (lines 209-256)\\n\\nThe `setPodHostAndAnnotations()` function performs a `GuaranteedUpdate` in etcd that:\\n- Sets the pod's `spec.nodeName` to the target node\\n- Updates pod annotations\\n- Sets the `PodScheduled` condition to True\\n- Returns the updated pod object\\n\\n### 4. Kubelet Pod Discovery from API Server (pkg/kubelet/config/apiserver.go)\\nOnce a pod is bound to a node, the kubelet discovers it through the API server source:\\n- `NewSourceApiserver()` (lines 37-54) creates a field selector for pods matching the node's name\\n- It uses a `ListWatcher` to watch pods where `spec.nodeName` matches the kubelet's node\\n- `newSourceApiserverFromLW()` (lines 57-68) creates a `Reflector` that watches the API server and sends `PodUpdate` events to the kubelet's config channel\\n- Updates are sent with operation type `kubetypes.SET` to the kubelet's pod config system\\n\\n### 5. Pod Admission Gates (pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/interfaces.go and predicate.go)\\nBefore a bound pod is started, the kubelet invokes pod admission handlers defined in:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/interfaces.go` defines the `PodAdmitHandler` interface (line 41-44), `PodAdmitAttributes` (lines 21-28), and `PodAdmitResult` (lines 30-38)\\n- `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/predicate.go` implements `predicateAdmitHandler` which validates:\\n  - Node availability and node info\\n  - CPU and memory availability\\n  - Pod OS/architecture compatibility\\n  - Init container restart policies\\n  - Storage and resource constraints\\n\\n### 6. Pod Admission in Kubelet (pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go)\\nThe kubelet's `canAdmitPod()` method (lines 2348-2352):\\n- Retrieves all currently allocated pods on the node\\n- Creates `PodAdmitAttributes` with the pod being evaluated and other pods\\n- Iterates through registered `admitHandlers` (line 2355)\\n- Returns false if any handler rejects the pod, preventing it from being started\\n\\n### 7. Pod Synchronization (pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go)\\nOnce a pod is admitted, the kubelet's `SyncPod()` method (lines 1844-1848):\\n- Receives the pod from the config system\\n- Orchestrates container creation, volume mounting, and networking\\n- Manages the pod's lifecycle through to completion\\n\\n### Complete Flow Summary\\nThe chain flows as follows:\\n1. Scheduler's `bindingCycle()` calls `DefaultBinder.Bind()`\\n2. Binder makes REST call to API server: `Pods.Bind(binding)`\\n3. API server's `BindingREST.Create()` updates pod with `spec.nodeName`\\n4. Kubelet's API server watcher detects the bound pod via `NewSourceApiserver()` reflector\\n5. Pod is passed to `canAdmitPod()` which runs `PodAdmitHandler` gates\\n6. If admitted, `SyncPod()` is called to manage the pod's runtime lifecycle\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that scheduler decisions are properly propagated to the kubelet through the API server, with intermediate admission checks at the kubelet level to guarantee the pod can actually run on the node before containers are started.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Scheduler's `bindingCycle()` calls `DefaultBinder.Bind()`\\n2. Binder makes REST call to API server: `Pods.Bind(binding)`\\n3.
